Yesterday (27th) held a large-scale literacy movement parade. At 3:00 p.m., soldiers from the 1st and 2nd Regiments of the Suzhou Garrison, public security police teams, business community self-defense teams, primary and secondary school students, Sun Yat-sen Boy Scouts, and various mass organizations gathered at the public sports field and departed. They passed through Wusa Road, Gongxiang, Guanqian Street, Lindun Road, Baitazi Lane, East-West Central City, Zhongjie Road, Jingde Road, exited Jinmen and dispersed to the road.

Wujiang Prison Guards Accused by All Staff 131

Liu Weilin, a prison guard in Wujiang County, was yesterday accused by all the staff of the prison to the Higher Court of deducting salaries, abusing parole and bail, fraud, and other charges. They requested that personnel be sent to thoroughly investigate. The Higher Court immediately sent personnel to investigate and verify the facts according to the report.

Zhenjiang Lawyer Hu Zhen Accused 132

Hu Zhen, a member of the Zhenjiang Lawyers Association, was recently sued by Ge Huaiqing, a client, to the Zhenjiang Procuratorate of the Higher Court for deception, intimidation of witnesses, and bribery. He requested that an investigation be carried out. After receiving the report, the Higher Procuratorate yesterday ordered the Zhenjiang District Court Procuratorate to investigate and reply for verification.

Wuxi

Case of Beating Wife to Death with Hoe Indicted 133

Huang Rongchu, a villager from Chengxiang, Tianshang City Bridge, Yanzhen, used an iron hoe to beat his wife, Shen, to death on the 26th of last month. Rongchu was detained and sent to the court for interrogation. It is learned that the case has been investigated by Zhou Erkai, the prosecutor of the Procuratorate. The act of the defendant Huang Rongchu beating his wife to death is suspected of violating Article 282, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, in accordance with Article 253, Paragraph 1 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, he was indicted to the Criminal Court of the same court for trial and sentencing.

Case of Inducing Intercourse Under the Guise of Marriage Heard in Court 134

Xue Fusun (formerly served in the military), a resident of Futian Lane in the city of the county, had a daughter named Lanzhen who was betrothed to Yao Runkun through a matchmaker. Unexpectedly, Yao Runkun suddenly reneged on the agreement, and Xue Fusun, because his daughter had been defiled by Runkun, filed a criminal lawsuit with the County Court, accusing him of inducing intercourse under the guise of marriage with a woman under the age of twenty, requesting that Yao be detained and dealt with according to law. The Procuratorate approved the acceptance, and the Chief Prosecutor Zhou summoned the plaintiff and defendant to court for interrogation the other day. As a result, the informant Xue Fusun was ordered to return, and the defendant Yao Runkun was released on bail.

Huaishang City Again Reports Robbery and Injury 135

The home of Zhang Xiaodi, a resident of Xujia Lane near Zhangjing Bridge in the seventh district of the county (Huaishang City), was suddenly visited by more than 20 robbers wearing white headscarves, straw sandals, and carrying hunting guns, iron blunderbusses, iron rulers, and flashlights at about 10:00 p.m. the other night. They broke into the house. At that time, the Zhang family was asleep. After the robbers entered the room, they tied up Xiaodi and his son Anan with ropes and burned their lower parts to force them to reveal the whereabouts of the hidden silver. Then they overturned boxes and cabinets and searched arbitrarily. After about three hours, they left with the stolen goods. A total of sixteen silver dollars and about four hundred yuan worth of gold and silver jewelry were robbed. When the robbers were leaving, they also trampled on the silkworm eggs and then swarmed to the home of Li Peihe to commit robbery, resulting in a loss of more than five hundred yuan. Now the victims, Zhang Xiaodi and Li Peihe, have not reported to the authorities to request an arrest. Furthermore, the home of Gu Rongbing, a villager in Nanyang Hetou Township in the same district, was also visited by more than 20 robbers at about 11:00 p.m. last night. They burst into the house to commit robbery and stabbed Rongbing in the left ear with a bayonet, leaving a wound about half an inch long. He immediately fell to the ground unconscious. The robbers then carried out a large-scale robbery and fired a shot before leaving with the stolen goods. After the incident, it was checked that the loss was more than five hundred yuan. The injured Huang Rongbing was carried to a nearby Western doctor for treatment and there was no danger to his life.

Cloth Weaving Industry Goes to Beijing to Petition for Exemption from Business Tax 136

The dyeing and weaving and knitting industries in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces believe that the products of these factories are directly woven from cotton yarn. Since cotton yarn has already paid the consolidated tax, and the direct burden is borne by the dyeing and weaving and knitting industries, it seems that the business tax should not be levied again. However, the business tax rate in Jiangsu Province is still included in the levy, which is indeed a duplicate tax. They have convened meetings of the industry several times in Shanghai and Wuxi to petition the Ministry of Finance to abolish it, but it has not been approved. They have convened another general meeting and appointed Cheng Jingtang and Ge Zicai from Wuxi, Zhu Wenqi and Pan Xuhua from Shanghai, and representatives from Jiangyin, Wujin, and Changshu to go to Beijing yesterday to petition the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry.

The Japanese ship Yijin Maru collided with and sank Xu Huiyuan's cargo ship in the Nantong Ren Port River. County Magistrate Zhang and Zhang, the District Chief of the Fourth Water Police District, have submitted the case to the province and consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the Japanese ambassador. All sectors of the local community held a meeting at the County Party Headquarters on the 26th and telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to support them.

The Coastal Defense Office of the Pacification Commissioner's Office of the Provincial Government, in order to protect the fishing season in the coastal areas of northern Jiangsu, has established an office in Tongzhou. The fishery protection period is provisionally limited to two months, and it will be revoked as soon as the sea is calm. The funding for this fishery protection and pirate suppression is allocated 20,000 yuan from the provincial treasury.

Jiangyin

Trade Associations Appeal for Postponement of Business Tax Collection 141

All trade associations in the county, believing that the Provincial Government's resolution to levy business tax from April 1st, as ordered by the Finance Department, is unacceptable before the relevant regulations are amended by the Legislative Yuan, are resolved not to acknowledge and pay it. Therefore, at 2 p.m. on the 25th, a joint meeting was held at the silk and cloth association. After discussion, the following resolutions were made: (1) Jointly telegraph the Central Yuan, ministries, and Jiangsu Provincial Department to appeal for instructions to postpone the collection; (2) Temporarily suspend the filling and submission of declaration forms; (3) Take measures to investigate, etc., and temporarily refuse. Furthermore, the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Cotton Textile Industry Joint Association, believing that cotton weaving has already borne the cotton yarn consolidated tax as stipulated by the central government and should not be subject to business tax again, has initiated a joint effort by all trade associations in the cotton textile industries of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to petition the central ministries in Beijing to remove the cotton weaving industry from the business tax regulations and exempt it from taxation. Wu Shuying, chairman of the cotton cloth industry in Jiangyin, and Yin Zhaoyong, chairman of the native cloth industry, are scheduled to go to Beijing on the 26th to petition.

Seven Families Robbed in Xiaosanbaocun Village 142

In Xiaosanbaocun village outside the south gate, seven farming families, including Zhang Jukun, Zhang Shengbao, Zhang Shengyang, Zhang Wubao, Zhang Wenbao, Zhang Baoquan, and Zhang Yizhi, lived together in one house. At around 3 a.m. on the 25th, more than ten robbers armed with rifles and Mauser pistols broke into the house and robbed the seven families, causing significant losses. Afterwards, the South Gate Public Security First Sub-station reported the incident to the General Bureau, which transferred it to the county for handling. It is also reported that Father Shen, a Catholic priest from Changshu Catholic Church, came to Cheng on the 24th to visit a friend at the Muyizhuang Catholic Church in Changshou. At around 10 p.m. that night, he was robbed of 400 yuan he was carrying, and he was kidnapped along with the money. Yesterday, the Public Security Bureau ordered Fan Gongzhi, the head of the detective team, to assist in the investigation.

Volunteer Corps Captures Bandits 147

On the 24th of this month, the First District Corps Headquarters of the Jiashan Protection Corps received a tip from a secret agent that bandits from Dabang were plotting to rob the Yaozhuang Bridge area. Li Tuanzong, upon receiving the report, immediately led Zhou Zhuli, along with volunteer corps members and militiamen, to set out. Upon arriving at the location, the bandits had already fled after hearing the news. The next morning, they pursued the bandits to the Nanke Village area and engaged in a fierce battle for an hour. Jiaxing

Second Squad of the Fifth Water Police Team Disarmed 148

The Second Squad of the Fifth Water Police Team in the Second District of Jiaxing was stationed in Zhouquan Town, which belongs to Chongde County. During the recent looting of Shiwan by bandits, the Zhouquan Water Police cooperated with the local land police to jointly pursue the bandits. Later, when the Water Police encountered the bandits, both sides opened fire. The land police then withdrew to the town under the pretext of maintaining local order. Subsequently, the Water Police intercepted a bandit boat filled with ornaments. The squad leader reported this to District Chief Zhou, who in turn reported it to the Provincial Bureau. Unexpectedly, the Chongde County authorities reported the incident to the Provincial Bureau, which dispatched patrol officers and police from the shallow-water warship to Zhouquan the day before yesterday to disarm the entire Second Squad of the Fifth Water Police Team. On the one hand, District Chief Zhou from the provincial capital was informed. On the 26th, the squad leaders of the Water Police team jointly issued a guarantee to District Chief Zhou, requesting him to forward it to the Provincial Bureau, stating that the squad leader of the Second Squad had rendered meritorious service in suppressing the bandits, and they were willing to jointly take responsibility and guarantee that the firearms would be returned and they would continue to perform their duties as usual. It is unknown how the Provincial Bureau will handle this matter.

Shangyu

Severe Meningitis in the Southeast Regions 149

Meningitis suddenly broke out in Zhang Village in the southern region at the beginning of this month, spreading to places like Ma Village and Zhou Ao, causing over four deaths.

The disease starts with cold followed by fever, or fever followed by cold, or vomiting and diarrhea. Death occurs within a day and night. It has recently spread to the eastern region. Most of those affected are young children. It is estimated that over twenty people have died in each of the villages along the Siming River, Yonghe, and Hengshan. The local officials are procuring camphor, brandy, and special medicines for meningitis from Shanghai and Yuyao for the villagers to obtain and use for treatment. They have also requested the Weisheng Hospital in the city to send doctors to the affected villages to administer vaccinations to reduce the risk. The county government has also telegraphed the Civil Affairs Department to allocate funds to purchase medicines for relief.

Pinghu

Man Revives After Being Electrocuted 150

The electric lights installed in the Shenghua Sock Factory on the Xitaiping Bridge embankment outside the West Gate suddenly leaked electricity last night. A worker in the factory was electrocuted and collapsed, seemingly dead. The factory workers panicked and were at a loss, unable to find a way to help him. After lying motionless for a while, the electricity dissipated, and the worker suddenly sat up, miraculously reviving. The factory workers were overjoyed.

Bandit Executed by Firing Squad for Kidnapping surnamed Ding 151

Wu Ajin, a fierce bandit under Liu Dexing, a bandit in the eastern region, previously kidnapped the young son of Ding Shenghe, a farmer from the Hanjiamiao Hanjiazhai area, demanding a ransom of 3,000 yuan. Later, the bandit lair was uncovered by the Sanyihe Protection Corps, and the son was rescued. The bandit Wu Ajin was identified by the victim and captured. The county government sentenced him to twelve years in prison. However, someone appealed to the provincial authorities, who resentenced him to death. Therefore, the county government escorted him to the execution ground at the foot of the South Gate city wall at 8:30 a.m. on the 27th and executed him by firing squad.

Jinchang and Dasheng in the Sigubiao township and Zhenxin in Xintai township. The county government will persuade other factories to open their doors to provide relief to farmers' silk harvests.

Education News

Special Article

Attention That Should Be Paid to the Advocacy of Vocational Education by Yang Weiyu 153

"Backward social production and people's livelihood difficulties" are indeed the current situation in our country, and what is most regrettable is the increasing number of graduates from schools who are unemployed in society. These people are scattered in society, their knowledge and desires have surpassed ordinary people, but they do not have any specialized skills. They aspire to climb high but have no means to make a living. They are filled with sorrow, and society is wary of them. This phenomenon is a hidden concern for the future of the country. Recently, the Ministry of Education, recognizing the root cause and promoting its benefits and harms, has widely announced to the whole country. The most important sentence is: "For thirty years, our country has been running schools, but social production has lagged behind and people's livelihood has become increasingly difficult. The reason is that ordinary schools have never paid attention to vocational education..." This statement is to the point and truly resonates with my heart. Those of us who have long advocated "vocational education" and campaigned for it in society, once we see this clear instruction, our joy and encouragement are indescribable. We wish for the success of vocational education from the start. It is not that we have a private interest in our usual advocacy, but that it is truly in the best interest of the country and society to do so.

However, nothing in the world is absolute. Often, where there is benefit, there is also harm. Therefore, in the midst of the Ministry of Education's great advocacy for vocational education, I have a sense of both joy and fear. For thirty years, our country has indeed not paid attention to vocational education. However, between 1916 and 1926, the call for vocational education also reached a high pitch. Industrial schools of types A and B were even established in various provinces and regions. But how long did it last? They were reorganized and closed one after another. Although the reasons for their reorganization and closure varied, they were at least due to the difficulty of both talent and money. Due to insufficient funds, the equipment was crude and simple. Due to insufficient talent, the disadvantage of using people in ways that did not suit their strengths arose. Ten years of operation yielded no results. Those with superficial knowledge did not understand the reasons for the failure and instead blamed "vocational education" as being inappropriate. Administrative authorities who generally feared difficulties used this opportunity to hide their shortcomings. "Vocational education" was truly not valued during these five years. "Vocational education" suffered this injustice, which is truly a great misfortune.

Running education is difficult, but running vocational education is even more difficult, as everyone recognizes. Because it is particularly difficult, few people dare to run it, and even fewer succeed. This is due to the difficulty of running it and the improper methods, which has nothing to do with vocational education itself. The difficulty of running vocational education lies in the need for adequate equipment and specialized professors. For industry, there is a need for factories; for agriculture, there is a need for farms; and for commerce, there is a need for appropriate practice grounds. Other school equipment can be crude and simple, but vocational schools must not be incomplete. Professors must also have specialized talents and not only have the ability to teach clearly but also have practical experience. In other words, they must not only be able to "teach" but also be able to "do." This is even more difficult than ordinary schools and absolutely cannot be compromised. Other aspects, such as the standards for setting up schools, the selection of teaching materials, the methods of practice, the promotion of career paths, the training policies, and the teaching methods, can all be said to have "no predecessors to learn from." Everything requires precise investigation and detailed research. Therefore, there must be sufficient preparation, cultivating teachers on the one hand and raising funds on the other. Only then can orders be issued and actions be taken effectively. Otherwise, once it is greatly advocated and the whole country blindly follows suit, from the twentieth year onwards, the trend will be that schools will change from the past, when they changed from vocational to ordinary, to changing from ordinary to vocational. There will inevitably be arbitrary reorganizations without standards. The content will inevitably be nominal without substance. The example of the former type A and B industrial schools will be repeated, causing "vocational education" to suffer injustice again and betraying the enthusiasm of the gentlemen of the Ministry of Education. This is something we do not want to hear.

Therefore, in addition to joyfully encouraging it, I humbly hope that the educational administrative authorities and those who actually run schools will pay attention to the following points when setting up or reorganizing vocational schools:

1. Establish departments that adapt to the school's environment.

2. Estimate the school's economic capacity and equip accordingly.

3. First, seek suitable teachers.

4. Predict future career paths.

5. Investigate the social conditions of the surrounding area.

6. Strive for contact with the vocational industry.

7. Have adequate practice grounds.

As for training policies, practice methods, textbook selection, and teaching methods, although the Ministry of Education already has design committees that will provide good models for learning in the future, they must also be adapted to local conditions and times and researched at any time and place. I have a more solemn statement: I say this out of a genuine desire to protect vocational education and a sincere hope for its success. I hope that the school authorities will not be timid because of my words and stop eating because of choking. Considering "vocational education" as the only way to solve the current livelihood and social problems and as an urgent and serious issue, strive to open up a new path for the education sector. It will not only be the fortune of the future of education but also the practical reliance of the country and society.

Ministry Order Dissolves Elementary Education Research Associations in Various Counties and Cities of Zhejiang 154

The Ministry of Education approved the letter from the Central Training Department to abolish the organizational standards of elementary education research associations in various counties and cities of Zhejiang Province. The Ministry of Education has instructed the Zhejiang Education Department to order all counties and cities to dissolve the already organized elementary education research associations. According to the party's guidance on the reorganization and organization of education associations, there is no need to establish education research associations separately after the establishment of education associations.

Zhejiang Finance Department to Allocate Another Half Month's Education Funds 155

Sufficient funds will be raised within days and transferred for collection.

Provincial Government Authorities Deeply Aware of the Plight of the Education Sector

Director Zhang of the Zhejiang Education Department previously discussed with the Finance Department the issue of organizing and issuing overdue education funds, agreeing to raise and issue funds for one and a half months. Currently, during the busy silkworm season for farmers, revenue from land taxes has been suspended. After the Finance Department allocated one month's education funds a few days ago, the provincial treasury has reached its limit. The Education Department is deeply aware of the overdue education funds and the difficult lives of colleagues in the education sector, and Secretary Shen of the Education Department took the opportunity to attend the provincial government meeting yesterday to present to Chairman Zhang of the provincial government the difficult lives of the education service personnel in the province. The Chairman was deeply moved and immediately instructed the Finance Department to strive to raise another half month's funding in a way that could not be arranged and to provide relief. It is said that the Finance Department will raise sufficient funds within days and allocate them to the Education Department for transfer to the various education institutions for collection. This is enough to demonstrate the efforts of the provincial financial authorities to take care of education.

Minutes of the Executive Committee Meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Teachers and Staff Union 156

The temporary meeting of the Executive Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Teachers and Staff Union was held at Zhenjiang Middle School on April 25th. Attendees included Xue Jianwu, Chen Yue, Wu Dezhang, Zhu Litian (representing Zhang Zhongyou), Wan Yixiang (representing Wu Cangsu), Wu Zixiu, and Zhang Shaonan (representing Dezhang). Wu Dezhang chaired the meeting, and Wu Zixiu recorded the minutes.

1. Chairman's Report: (1) The union should make a statement or express its views on the National Assembly. (2) The provincial schools' regular expenses have been in arrears for three months, and the union should find ways to expedite their release.

2. Matters for Discussion: (1) Proposal to petition the National Assembly to improve education in Jiangsu Province. Resolution: The key points of the petition are: (1) Financial issues: A. Reducing the expenses of Zhongda University should be borne by national taxes. Please order the Executive Yuan to effectively reorganize the Jiangsu Education Management Office. B. Opening up new sources of revenue: Please allocate a certain percentage of the cigarette tax to fund education in Jiangsu Province annually. Please allocate a certain percentage of the business tax in Jiangsu Province to fund education in Jiangsu Province. Recover the public forests owned by the Jiangsu Education Association. (2) Teachers and staff treatment issues: A. Increase hourly wages. B. Annual seniority increase. C. Children of teachers and staff can attend provincial secondary schools free of charge. D. Promulgate regulations on pensions and retirement funds. E. Provide housing for teachers and staff. (3) Improving educational efficiency issues: A. Stipulate regulations for provincial school teachers and staff to study abroad and visit foreign countries. B. Each provincial school should include academic research fees and domestic visiting fees in its budget. C. Utilize summer vacations to hold academic lectures, inviting domestic and foreign scholars to lecture by subject to improve the knowledge of secondary school teachers and staff. D. Carefully select educational administrators to ensure that knowledge is used and talents are put to good use. (4) Respect scholars and rectify the academic atmosphere. 2. Resolution on urging the release of overdue regular expenses for this semester: The Education Fee Management Office will be notified by the Union to release the funds for February and March before May 10th. If there are no results, a conference of fully authorized representatives from each school will be convened in Nanjing on May 18th to discuss solutions. (3) Resolution on whether teachers and staff should pay income tax: The Union will temporarily suspend the payment of income tax until the salaries of teachers and staff are increased. The Union will also write to the Secondary Education Research Association to investigate and ask Mr. Xia Peibai to draft an explanation of why teachers and staff should not pay income tax and publish it in the Union's Education Review. (4) The Party Ideology Research Conference decided to hold an inter-school Party Ideology speech contest on June 1st. The Union's executive resolution is to divide the competition into two groups: senior high school (male and female) and junior high school teachers (male and female). The date is June 1st, and the location is Wuxi Middle School. The judges are Gao Jianci, Yu Qingtang, Zhu Jingnong, Liu Luyin, Wu Zhihui, Qi Xiyong, Huang Yuren, Hu Nianqian, Hu Puan, Tong Hangbai, and Tao Baichuan. There will be one topic for senior and junior high schools each, and the Party Ideology teachers of Zhenjiang Middle School will be asked to draft the topics. The registration deadline is May 10th, and the schools participating should notify the Union before this date. The registration deadline is May 25th, and the number of winners will be three out of five or more in each group, and two out of five or less. Prizes, in addition to the prizes prepared by the Union itself (estimated at about 30 yuan), will also be raised from all sides. The schools participating should pay a fee of 10 yuan each, in accordance with the regulations of the second Secondary School Speech Contest. (5) The Union's regular meeting will be held on June 1st at Xizhong.

Jiangsu Provincial Literacy Campaign Week 157

Twenty-Five More Public Schools Added

The Jiangsu Provincial Literacy Campaign Week, which was held from the 20th to the 26th of this month, prepared various activities and publicity, making it an unprecedented event in the provincial capital. After the Literacy Campaign Week concluded, twenty-five public schools were added. The details are as follows:

<P First Day Opening Parade>

The opening ceremony was held on the first day at the county public sports ground. Over 50,000 people from organizations and the public participated. Director Chen Hexian of the Education Department presided over the ceremony, and Director Qi Xiyong of the preparation committee reported. Zhang Yuanyang, a member of the Provincial Party Department, and He Yushu, Director of the Agriculture and Mining Department, gave speeches. After the speeches, the participants paraded in a procession. In the evening, films were shown, and Liu Yungu, Director of the Nanjing Provincial Public Education Hall, gave a radio broadcast on the Central Radio Station, reporting on the overview of the Literacy Campaign.

Second Day Play and Games 158

The second day was dedicated to family publicity. The Wuxi Education College's special team for the Literacy Campaign gave lectures and games in different districts. Plays were performed on the stage of the Provincial Zhenjiang Public Education Hall, including "The Sale of People" and "A Patriotic Heart." Films were shown as usual. Registration for enrollment in public schools was carried out in different districts.

Third Day Group Publicity 159

The third day was dedicated to shop publicity. The expanded publicity teams organized by the Nanjing Provincial Public Education Hall, the Tangshan Farmers Education Hall, and the Zhenjiang Provincial Public Education Hall consisted of over 62 people, carrying gongs and drums and performing martial arts, which was very effective in attracting the public's attention. Games were still held at the sports ground. The Capital Public Theater Company, the Jiangsu Provincial Capital Theater Company, and the Zhenjiang Middle School Theater Company jointly performed four plays: "See Who Needs Who," "The Death of the Weather Vane," "The Beggar and the King," and "Oppression." Li Yunting gave a lecture on the Central Radio Station.

Fourth Day Car Parade 160

The fourth day was dedicated to factory publicity. The publicity teams focused on workers. Except for the games being held in Boxian Park, plays and famous people's speeches were given by Director Hu Puan of the Civil Affairs Department and President Gao Jianci of the Wuxi Education College. A car parade was held at 2 p.m.

Local News

Taxpayers Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Urging Improvement of Primary Education 166

20% of the Municipal Council's Revenue Should Be Used for Education

Yesterday, the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association sent a letter to the Public Concession Municipal Council, stating: "Respectfully, we received a letter from the Ningbo Association in Shanghai stating that the Concession is restricted by unequal treaties and that the governing power lies outside, which is heartbreaking. However, the education system is the lifeline of the country, and we Chinese must not give up through inertia. On March 26, 1928, your Council proposed that 20% of the Municipal Council's annual revenue be used for our Chinese education funds, which shows that you are enthusiastic about education and concerned about the country, which is admirable. However, in recent years, your Council has not fulfilled the aforementioned proposal for our Chinese education. Furthermore, according to the Municipal Council's Gazette of March 17 of this year, there are currently seven Chinese schools with only 3,281 students, which is 1,526 fewer than the 4,817 students in Western schools. The reason is that the schools set up by the Municipal Council are too expensive and do not meet the principle of education for the common people, and the education policy does not conform to the purpose of party-based education in our Republic of China. The Church has established eleven free schools for the purpose of cultivating the children of fellow villagers in Shanghai, and enrollment is free of charge. Although limited by funding and unable to expand as much as possible, the number of children in school now exceeds 4,000. The education policy implements the Three Principles of the People in teaching and various courses and extracurricular activities at all times and places, in order to achieve the effect of firm belief and practice and to cultivate the virtues of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace in the citizens. Therefore, based on the experience of our Association, on the one hand, we should proceed with diplomacy to recover the education rights of the Concession, and on the other hand, your Association should represent all our Chinese taxpayers to urge the Municipal Council to fulfill the proposal of March 26, 1928, to use 29% of the Municipal Council's annual revenue for our Chinese education funds and allow our Chinese to manage it ourselves. In response to this, the city has already sent a letter to your Council to handle the education issue diligently. In addition to replying to the letter, we are sending this letter to you for reference and joint handling."

Shanghai University Holds Annual Board Meeting 167

And Groundbreaking Ceremony for New Men's Dining Hall

Shanghai Hujiang University held its spring annual board meeting at the president's residence yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. Pan-Pacific Children's Games 168

China Will Be Invited to Join

The American Pacific Association, for the sake of international friendship among friendly nations along the Pacific coast, in conjunction with the Los Angeles Times newspaper, has decided to host a Pan-Pacific Children's Games, inviting China, Japan, Honolulu, Australia, New Zealand, and various American countries to join. The qualifications for athletes are children aged 9 to 16. Events include 60 meters, 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 1,500 meters, low hurdles, high hurdles, high jump, long jump, pole vault, shot put, discus, and javelin. The Japanese Ministry of Education has already received the association's official letter and has entrusted it to the Japanese Sports Association. China will also receive the association's official letter soon. However, the date of the games has not yet been determined and will be formally decided after replies from various countries. If China can prepare to participate, it will be an easy matter because the games are still far away, and now is the opportunity to train young people.

First Match of Sino-Western Handball 173

Chinese YMCA Unaccustomed to Venue | Loses to Western YMCA

The Chinese and Western YMCA agreed to hold the first match between handball players from the two associations yesterday at 6:00 PM at the Western YMCA to exchange skills. Many people came to watch. In terms of the strength of the players of the two teams, they were evenly matched. Because the Chinese YMCA was not accustomed to the venue at the beginning (the Western YMCA's court is bounded on all four sides, while the Chinese YMCA's court is only on three sides, so the ball often could not be returned when it hit the back wall) and the rules were different, the team members were not complete, and the score was often behind. Later, the venue became slightly familiar, and they learned the method and chased forward. However, the early birds had already flown ahead, and as a result, the Western YMCA won the Chinese YMCA by nine points to three points. It is reported that the second match is scheduled for next Monday (the 4th) at 6:00 PM at the Chinese YMCA. Because they wanted to become familiar with the association's court, they were willing to suffer losses and still play at the Western YMCA. Local News

Celebrating the National Assembly 181

Party and Government Agencies Decide to Organize Preparatory Committee Yesterday

Garrison Headquarters Instructed to Comply with Military Headquarters Order

The Shanghai Party and Government Agencies, in conjunction with various sectors, initiated a large-scale celebration of the National Assembly. The first consultation meeting was held yesterday (the 27th) at 2:00 PM. Chen Xunyu and Zhou Jisheng of the Municipal Government, Li Zheng and Zhou Hanmei of the Municipal Party Department, and others attended. The results of the meeting were to determine the following measures: (1) The name of the association was determined to be the Shanghai All Circles Celebration National Assembly Preparatory Committee. (2) The work outline of the association was determined and approved. (3) The office hours of the association were stipulated to be from 9:00 AM to 11:00 AM daily. (4) Persons in charge of custody and finance were designated to be Li Zheng. (5) Persons in charge of work were designated to be Zhou Jisheng and Zhou Hanmei for assembly matters, Zhou Hanmei and Chen Xunyu for entertainment and film matters, and Li Zheng and Chen Xunyu for editing matters. After the meeting adjourned, it was reported that the main points of the work outline set by the association were as follows: (1) The celebration meeting will be held at 9:00 AM on May 5th at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at Tianhougong Bridge. (2) The entertainment gala will be held from 7:00 PM on May 5th at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, inviting famous song and dance troupes and entertainment groups in the city to perform. (3) Film screenings will be held at 10:00 AM on May 5th, with six designated cinemas in the city showing films: Southeast and Penglai Theaters in the southern city area, Great Light and New Light Theaters in the central city area, and National World and New World Theaters in Zhabei. Other theaters and entertainment venues will also screen or post slogans celebrating the National Assembly. In terms of editing, there will be a special publication of propaganda slogans, etc. Major newspapers will publish special editions with articles written by prominent figures from the Party and government. The Songhu Garrison Headquarters received an order from the Ministry of Military Affairs yesterday, stating that in order to comply with the order, the Executive Yuan's telegraph stated (details omitted) that the central government had stipulated four measures for celebrating the National Assembly: (1) On the morning of May 5th, the local senior Party headquarters should convene organizations and groups to hold a celebration meeting of the National Assembly. (2) All localities nationwide should fly flags on May 5th to mark the celebration. (3) Local newspapers should add articles celebrating the National Assembly. (4) During the period of the National Assembly, Party headquarters at all levels should expand publicity for the National Assembly. In addition to the central government's telegram to the provincial and municipal Party headquarters for compliance, it is ordered that the aforementioned two methods be followed and that subordinates be ordered to comply accordingly. After receiving the order, the garrison headquarters ordered its subordinates to comply accordingly.

Members of the National Assembly Elected 182

Wu Kaixian Receives the Most Votes and Is Elected

Five Representatives Scheduled to Go to Beijing One After Another

The representatives of the National Assembly in this city have now been elected one after another. The Party member representatives opened the ballots yesterday at the Municipal Party Department, and Mr. Wu Kaixian received the most votes and was elected. Thus, all five representatives of this city were produced in accordance with the law. The details are recorded separately as follows.

Wu Kaixian Elected Party Member Representative 183

The National Party members in this city attending the National Assembly representatives from the 15th of this month to the 25th to convene party members' meetings (not limited to the legal number) designated by the Central Committee of the candidate Wu Kaixian (photo taken at Red Light Photo Studio)

One person was elected from among the people, and Comrade Huang Xuchu was elected as the election supervisor, and Zhang Yingzeng and others were elected as the voting administrators. Comrade Pan Gongzhan expressed to the Party Department before the election that he did not wish to be elected and strongly recommended Comrade Wu Kaixian to take on the arduous task. After receiving the order, the various branches proceeded with the election and it ended the day before yesterday (the 25th). The ballots were opened yesterday (the 27th) in the auditorium of the Municipal Party Department. Chen Bai was dispatched by the Election Office, and Tao Baichuan was dispatched by the Municipal Party Department as representatives to supervise the opening of the ballots. The ballot opening began at 10:00 AM and lasted until 1:00 PM. A total of 168 branches voted, with 1,828 votes cast. Da Chun, (photo taken at Red Light Photo Studio)

There were 1,799 valid votes and 29 invalid votes. Wu Kaixian received 1,605 votes, and Pan Gongzhan received 194 votes. As a result, Comrade Wu Kaixian received the most votes and was elected as the representative of the Shanghai Special Municipality of the Chinese Kuomintang to attend the National Assembly. Mr. Wu's brief biography is recorded as follows: Wu Kaixian is from Qingpu County, Jiangsu Province, and graduated from the Department of Economics of Shanghai Law College. In the 15th year of the Republic of China, he was elected as a representative to the Second National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang in Shanghai. In the 18th year, he was again elected as a representative to the Third National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang. He has served as a special administrator Chen Guansheng, (photo taken at Red Light Photo Studio)

Secretary of the Organization Department of the Shanghai Municipal Party Department, Member of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Affairs Guidance Committee and concurrently Minister of Organization, Member of the Executive Committee and concurrently Minister of Organization of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, and currently Member of the Executive Committee and concurrently Standing Committee Member of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department.

The labor union representative to the National Assembly of this city, Hou Dachun, and the farmers' association representative, Chen Guansheng, are scheduled to go to Beijing on the second of next month. The chamber of commerce representative, Wang Yansong, and the party headquarters representative, Wu Kaixian, are scheduled to go to Beijing on the second or third of next month to attend the National Assembly. Business Community Pays Attention to National Assembly Proposals 185

The Proposal Review Committee of the Business Community of this city held its second committee meeting yesterday. The resolutions were as follows: (1) The resolution of the Lishi Industry Representative Conference and the three resolutions of the First Committee Meeting were all reviewed and the reasons and methods were approved. (2) The proposal of the Hu Shuhua

the industry association requested the National Assembly to urge the government to strictly prohibit the use of the old calendar in order to facilitate the unification of the period for businesses. It was resolved that an order has already been issued, so there is no need to propose it. (3) The proposal of the industry association requested the National Assembly to deliberate on a unified monetary system plan and order the government to implement it within a time limit. It was resolved that it would be approved for submission. (4) Jin Chuxiang proposed that protection should be given to civil vessels damaged by steamships to benefit the shipping industry. It was resolved to merge with the proposal of the Industry and Commerce Conference. (5) Jin Chuxiang proposed to strictly prevent Japanese investment in China's fishing industry. It was resolved that the government is handling it, so there is no need to propose it. (6) Jin Chuxiang proposed that the continuous rise in housing prices places a heavy burden on merchants and people. It was resolved that there is no need to propose it. The proposal of the advertising industry association requested that an order be issued to abolish the advertising tax. It was resolved to merge it. (8) The proposal of the cotton cloth industry association proposed that the use of stamps on tax payment certificates should be abolished immediately. It was resolved to merge it. (9) The proposal of the cotton cloth industry association proposed to add compulsory schools and to increase the number of free places in each middle school and university in order to popularize education and cultivate talents. It was resolved to submit the last proposal and the meeting was adjourned.

Mr. Wang Yansong (Photo taken at Red Light Photo Studio) 186

Labor Representative Hou Dachun Speaks 187

The National News Agency reporter visited Hou Dachun, the standing supervisor of the Shanghai Publishing Industry Union, who is the labor representative this time, to inquire about his views on the National Assembly. Mr. Hou graciously met with the reporter and answered the questions one by one. The main points are summarized below. Mr. Hou said that the National Assembly is an unprecedented grand event that will benefit the Party and the country and benefit the people's livelihood. All the workers in the city are determined to sincerely support it and witness its success. Although we workers occupy an important position in the production sector, we have never had the opportunity to participate in politics. Since the Republic of China, although elections for councilors have been held in various places, due to the poor electoral system, the regional representative system has been adopted, which is mostly controlled by wealthy gentlemen and landlords. As a result, workers have been excluded. Since the National Government moved to Nanjing and implemented the political tutelage and construction, industry and commerce conferences and other important conferences related to labor have been held, but labor representatives have never been invited to attend and participate, so that the opinions of the workers have not been contributed, resulting in many gaps. I personally regret this very much. The holding of this National Assembly is based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy and adopts a professional representative system. We workers can then fully enjoy the right to elect and be elected, and can freely express all opinions in the meeting, which is truly a pioneering event for Chinese workers to participate in politics. It is a pity that the preparation period for the National Assembly was too short, and many labor unions in Shanghai have not yet completed the reorganization, so the number of people who gave up the election or did not have time to participate in the election is still large. However, observing the psychology of the workers in the city, they are all wholeheartedly supporting the National Assembly. As for the proposals of the workers in this city to the National Assembly, they are being actively prepared recently, and there is an organization called the National Assembly Shanghai Workers' Proposal Research Association, which is presided over by the talented people in the labor industry of this city. The research content includes requesting the National Assembly to automatically declare the abolition of all unequal treaties, requesting the National Assembly to determine the policy of converting soldiers into workers based on Dr. Sun Yat-sen's legacy, establishing a labor department, promulgating a special labor union law, determining the implementation of a labor education plan, formulating a labor insurance system, providing relief to unemployed workers, and amending various laws that are detrimental to labor welfare, etc. In the end, the individual has followed the workers of the city and struggled to this day without fail. I am deeply apprehensive about being elected as a representative by the love of the workers of the city. I believe that I am shallow in scholarship, weak in strength, and lacking in ability to be competent. However, in the face of great righteousness, I should do my best, but my own ability is limited, and I still rely on the full guidance of the workers of the city to achieve complete success.

Customs Brokerage Industry Resumes Work Yesterday 192

Cotton Cloth Cargo Fully Restored One Day Exporting 6,000 Pieces

Cotton Cloth Industry to Refuse to Pay Dockage Fee Generating Problems

After the customs workers in this city followed the order to resume work yesterday, all cotton cloth cargo to the East and West Oceans was restored. Because cotton cloth merchants refused to pay the dockage fee, a meeting will be held today to discuss the matter. The various situations are recorded separately below.

Resumption of Transportation Situation 193

After receiving the trade union notice, the customs workers all went to resume work yesterday morning. Because the consignors have been on strike until now, the inventory has been sold out, and the goods are urgently needed. The various scheduled goods were all rushed for export yesterday, totaling more than 6,000 pieces. Cotton goods are piled up like mountains at Mitsubishi Wharf, Second Avenue Wharf, New Wharf, Jardine Wharf, etc. The customs workers are extremely busy, and the police authorities have dispatched additional patrols to maintain traffic at the various wharves.

Another Problem Arises 194

The tobacco industry customs brokers convened a general meeting at Tongjulong Customs Brokerage on Tianzhutang Street yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM to discuss the cotton cloth industry's refusal to pay the dockage fee. All 15 companies, including Yishun Heng, unanimously advocated that a letter be sent to the industry association immediately to convene a general meeting of all customs brokers and to suggest to the association that the dockage fee should be collected by the cotton cloth merchants no matter what. If the cotton cloth industry insists, all transportation will be suspended from today.

Emergency Meeting 195

Because the cotton cloth merchants of each company that the customs brokers were carrying yesterday uniformly refused to pay the dockage fee, and the consignors could not agree, they temporarily paid it and reported it to the association, requesting strict negotiations. The Customs Brokers Association notified all colleagues yesterday that a meeting would be held today to discuss the matter. Because the matter of the cotton cloth industry refusing to pay the dockage fee is related to the interests of the industry, an emergency meeting will be convened tomorrow (the 28th) at 3:00 PM at Qingyunli for public discussion. It is hoped that you will attend at that time.

Union Thanks 196

The Customs Brokers Union sent a letter to the various unions yesterday, stating that it was grateful for the sympathy and support. Since the strike of the union, it has been more than two weeks. The Social Bureau has mediated several times without success. On the 24th, the final mediation reached a satisfactory resolution and revised the draft agreement, so that the inherent precedents of decades were not destroyed. Although the matter was handled impartially by the Social Bureau, it was also due to your honorable words of advice and the spirit of fearlessness of Mr. Sun Yat-sen to fight. Therefore, I hereby send a letter of thanks. The union has already ordered the resumption of work on the 27th.

Sending Ships to Carry Unemployed Overseas Workers from Giant Port Back to China 197

Totaling 352 People

Ministry of Industry and Communications Are Negotiating

There are quite a few Chinese in Giant Port. Recently, due to various restrictions, the majority are unemployed, and some cannot live there for a day. The consul in the port, in view of this situation, repeatedly telegraphed the national government to request relief. The Ministry of Industry is currently negotiating to send ships to carry these distressed overseas workers back to China. The details are recorded separately below.

Consul Cai Reports 198

Consul Cai Xianzhang stationed in Giant Port reported to the Ministry of Industry of the National Government, stating that the Research and Art Machinery Union of Giant Port requested relief and forwarded it to the National Government for appropriation of travel expenses to summon unemployed overseas Chinese workers to return to China, etc. Minister Kong telegraphed Cai to order him to investigate and report the number and situation of unemployed workers in the area. After the report, it was stated that according to the report of the union, there were 322 unemployed workers, and another 30 workers' families and children. The estimated travel expenses required are about 60,000 yuan in national currency, which is really a large amount. At this time, the national treasury is empty, and I am deeply afraid that it will be difficult to do so. I think it is better to send a domestic commercial ship to carry the unemployed overseas workers back, which will save national currency and can also try sailing the Nanyang route, which is a good thing to do. Is it feasible to transfer the inquiry to the Ministry of Communications for review and implementation.

Ministry of Industry Transfers Ship 199

After Minister Kong telegraphed his report, he consulted the Ministry of Transportation, stating roughly that, according to Consul Cai's report, the proposed dispatch of a ship to transport unemployed Chinese laborers back from Ju'gang (Jakarta) would benefit both worker relief and shipping development, and the plan was indeed appropriate. However, the dispatch of commercial ships falls under your ministry's jurisdiction. Therefore, he consulted with you to investigate and reply. The Ministry of Transportation then informed the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, stating that the Consul's request to send a ship to transport overseas Chinese laborers from Ju'gang back to China was for the purpose of saving national currency and providing relief to workers, which was indeed feasible. However, the company should consider whether there were any ships available for dispatch, so that they could reply to the Consul.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Deliberation 200

Regarding the issue of dispatching a ship, the Ministry of Transportation mainly suggested that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company allocate a ship. However, sending an empty ship to Ju'gang would be a great sacrifice. It would be best to also load goods and passengers to that location, so that freight charges could be collected to compensate for the cost. This matter still needs to await the return of Commissioner Li Zhonggong to Shanghai to discuss and determine a plan before a final decision and telegram reply to Ju'gang.

Liu Jinshan, a worker at the Romek Sugar Factory, was brutally beaten by a White Russian named Mirikovsk at 8:30 AM on March 11th and sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. He passed away in the hospital at 8:00 AM on the 24th of this month after more than a month. He is survived by his elderly mother in her sixties, a young widow, and two orphans under the age of five, a truly pitiful situation. Representatives of the factory workers, Jiang Dechen, Xiao Huanzhang, Li Shujun, Jiang Zongguan, Li Shouji, Liu Yiqing, Zhang Kerong, Sun Lin, Meng Qingxian, Cheng Yongshu, Ling Asan, Gao Shouyun, and others, issued a declaration. The original text is very long; excerpts are as follows: "Dear workers and people from all walks of life, Worker Liu's family includes a white-haired mother in her sixties and a young widow, as well as two orphans under the age of five, all of whom depended on Worker Liu's hard-earned money for support. The brutal attacker has not only directly harmed Worker Liu personally but has also indirectly harmed his entire family's life. Who would not be heartbroken by this situation? (Middle omitted) At a time when the National Assembly is approaching and civil rights are being promoted, the perpetrators of this heinous act have dared to flaunt their cruelty and inflict such brutal treatment, leading to the death of our fellow worker. Anyone with a shred of conscience cannot help but be outraged. We hope that our fellow workers and people from all walks of life will provide strong support to our factory. This is not just a matter for the workers of our factory but a matter of concern for all workers in Shanghai. The workers of our factory solemnly declare to all labor unions, workers, and people from all walks of life that we must work together to strive for humanity and protect the safety of all workers in Shanghai. Our factory proposes: (1) Immediately execute the detained Mirikovsk as retribution. (2) Immediately punish the Romek factory owner who condoned the violence. (3) The factory owner must immediately compensate for all losses suffered by Worker Liu. (4) The factory owner must immediately provide for Worker Liu's family. (5) Guarantee that the same incident will not occur again in the future."

Stamp Duty Required for Rent Receipts 213

Court Notice: Landlords Take Note

The Shanghai Special District Stamp Tax Office previously issued a letter to the Special District Local Court requesting assistance in the matter of landlords in the concessions continuing to delay in affixing stamp duty to rent receipts. The letter stated that if there were any cases of rent arrears lawsuits, those rent receipts that had not been affixed with stamp duty would be punished according to regulations, as a warning to others. It is now known that the court has issued a notice to all landlords to comply. The original text is as follows: "The Jiangsu Shanghai Special District Local Court issues a notice regarding the matter of a letter received from the Shanghai Special District Stamp Tax Office of the Jiangsu Stamp, Tobacco, and Alcohol Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, stating, 'Since the establishment of our office, we have been greatly assisted by your court in promoting stamp tax affairs, which has enabled smooth progress and increased tax revenue. We are extremely grateful. However, in the matter of rent receipts, stamp duty should be affixed in accordance with regulations. Currently, many landlords in the concessions are complying with regulations, but there are also many who are delaying compliance. In addition to our office sending personnel to provide earnest guidance and carry out thorough rectification, we plan to request that your court, in cases of rent arrears lawsuits, immediately punish those rent receipts that have not been affixed with stamp duty according to regulations and order them to affix supplementary stamp duty as a warning to others. This will ensure that cunning individuals are deterred from engaging in evasive practices and that the future of national tax revenue will greatly benefit. Accordingly, we send this letter to your court, requesting that you investigate and comply, and we hope to receive a reply.' After the letter was received by our court, in addition to replying to the letter, we issue this notice to inform all parties concerned. This notice.'"

Taxpayers Association Pleads for Rickshaw Pullers 221

Police Tear Up Permits, Confiscate Cushions

Not a Method to Maintain Traffic

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday to help rickshaw pullers, stating: "Sir, according to Mr. Squire's letter, I have repeatedly sought to improve the living conditions of rickshaw pullers, but with little effect. I am writing to you in the hope that you will be fair and provide assistance. From my window in the Sassoon House, I see Chinese police officers forcibly pointing out rickshaw pullers for violating traffic regulations and tearing up their permits and confiscating the cushions from their rickshaws. I have written to Mr. Masesson of the Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers Gospel Society to warn the rickshaw pullers of the dangers of soliciting business on the road. Mr. Ma replied that this is the responsibility of the police. I have written to the police station, and they have promised to consider it. I have also printed flyers and distributed them every morning to the Chinese police officers standing at the entrance of the Huizhong Hotel, but the tearing up of permits and the confiscation of cushions continues to occur daily. In these times of economic downturn, I cannot bear the cruel treatment of the poor rickshaw pullers. Can your council provide assistance in this matter?" The association investigated and found that the police tearing up permits and confiscating cushions from rickshaw pullers has become commonplace. The only reason given is that the rickshaw pullers are disrupting traffic regulations. However, many police officers are arbitrarily tearing up permits and confiscating cushions to gain merit. The association believes that traffic regulations should be maintained, but tearing up permits and confiscating cushions is not the best way to maintain traffic regulations. Furthermore, when police officers tear up permits and confiscate cushions, those who are not being torn up will pull their rickshaws wildly and crash around in an attempt to escape, while those who have been torn up will kowtow to the police officers like pounding garlic or even have to meet their certain needs in order to have their permits and cushions returned on the spot. At this time, traffic order is not maintained but rather lost, which is not the right way to do things. Therefore, the association believes that Mr. Squire's proposal is very correct and sends this letter to you in the hope that you will investigate and handle it accordingly.

Robbers Open Fire and Wound People on Lan Ni Du 222

Looks Like a Revenge Killing

They Fled Without Stealing Anything

In Ni Cai’s (a Ningbo native) small tobacco and paper shop near the Bingchangtian ice factory on Nanchang East Road in Pudong’s Lan Ni Du town, two uninvited guests suddenly arrived the night before last. One stood outside as a lookout, and the other went inside, pulled out a handgun, and opened fire, wounding Ni’s son, Amao, in the face, but not fatally. The police station’s investigation determined that it was likely a revenge killing. Yesterday, they submitted a report to the Public Security Bureau, requesting an order to arrest the perpetrators. Here are the details of the investigation:

Gun Pulled Out and Fired 223

Ni, 51 years old, has been running a small tobacco and paper shop at No. 16 Bingchangtian for several years. His family also lives there. The small business is enough to cover expenses. At 7:00 PM the night before last, after dinner, Ni and his son, Amao (18 years old), were chatting in the shop when a middle-aged man of small stature suddenly entered, wearing a dark blue long gown, a solid-colored woolen vest, and a pointed hat. Another person stood outside as a lookout. The person who entered first took out two small silver coins and said he wanted to buy cigarettes. Ni had just recovered from an illness and was hard of hearing and slow to respond. The man became angry and twisted Ni's collar with his left hand, reached into his pocket with his right hand, pulled out a handgun, and pointed it at his son Amao's head, pulling the trigger. With a "pop" sound, the bullet entered his right cheek near the ear and exited through his right mouth. The perpetrator, seeing that his goal had been achieved, immediately fled outside.

Cousin Seems Suspicious 224

When Li Tianfu, a guard from the No. 3 District of the Public Security Bureau, arrived after hearing the report, he saw Amao's face covered in blood and immediately took him to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. After the doctor's examination, it was determined that the bullet had exited and the injury was not fatal. Zhang, the district chief, used the telephone to notify the No. 4 Squad to send officers to various locations to search, but the perpetrator had already disappeared. They then returned to Ni's small shop to investigate the situation and found a bullet casing on the ground. Ni stated that nothing in the shop was lost, and he had no enemies except for his cousin, Ni Shangen, with whom he had not been in contact for 18 years. He suddenly came to his house the week before last, wanting to borrow 50 yuan, but only ate a meal and left in a huff. It is not known whether he held a grudge and sought to kill his son. The district chief determined that the case was not a robbery but rather a revenge killing. Yesterday, he reported the details to the Public Security Bureau, requesting an order to arrest the perpetrators and bring them to justice.

Continued Hearing on the Case of the Liquidator of the Riya Bank Pursuing Debts 227

Wu Cheng and Pan Zhaobang, the liquidators of the Shanghai Riya Bank, filed a lawsuit in the French Court against more than ten households, including the Samsung Stage, Samsung Real Estate Company, Taiheyuan, Nanjing Sock Factory, and Hangzhou Restaurant, for failing to pay their debts to the Riya Bank, requesting that they be recovered in full. Yesterday, Zhao Ruquan of the Samsung Stage was summoned and retained a lawyer to argue that the Samsung Stage did indeed owe money to the Riya Bank, but that more than 1,000 yuan and 250 taels of silver were paid on behalf of Huang Chu Jiu and should be deducted. As for the Samsung Real Estate Company, it was jointly organized by Zhao Ruquan, Zhou Bingchen, and Huang Chu Jiu, and each person should pay 20,000 yuan in capital. The contract stated that if there were any profits, the three would share them equally. It is now found that the company has paid out more than 180,000 taels of the Riya Bank's money, which should be the responsibility of Huang Chu Jiu to return. There are ledgers to prove this. The judge ordered that the accounts be verified first. Someone on behalf of Taiheyuan said that the money had been paid to the guarantor and taken away. The judge ordered the guarantor to be summoned for further questioning. The Nanjing Sock Factory refused to sign. The judge ordered a summons to be issued for the case to be pursued. The manager of the Hangzhou Restaurant stated that he admitted to owing money, but that the Riya Bank owed a shareholder 1,600 yuan, which he requested permission to deduct. Accountant Pan stood up to object. The judge adjourned the hearing to one month.

Verdict in Xinli Major Theft Case 228

Three Police Officers Each Sentenced to Two Years and Eight Months

The previous report detailed the trial of Fei Guangqing and Cheng Yingzhou, watchmen police officers of the British Xinli Foreign Firm on Nanjing Road, who conspired with Zhao Tingrong, a police officer from the Putuo Road Police Station, and others to steal a large number of fashionable watches from the firm. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu of the Special District Local Court sentenced Fei, Cheng, and Zhao to two years and eight months of imprisonment each. If they are unable to pay the fines, they may be commuted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. Yang Huizhi was found not guilty.

Homeowner and Servant of a Village Head Robbed and Tragically Killed 229

Shajin Village in the second excited town's southern sands area of Haimen County, north of Wusong, the chief of the village, Sha Jinzao's family had saved a bit of money leading to it being coveted by bandits, The night before last around eight o'clock suddenly ten or more bandits, mostly speaking the local dialect, each holding handguns and electric torches, broke down the door and entered, first driving the family members to a room and confining them, then twisting Sha Jinzao, beating him and extorting silver dollars because Sha's speech was hesitant, the bandits shot him dead. They then ransacked the house, taking all the clothes and other stolen goods, and ordered Sha's servant, Fan Chaohai, to tie them up for them. Fan refused, and was also shot dead by the bandits. Then they left Yangchang. The family members, knowing the bandits were gone, came out and saw that the two had fallen to the ground in a pool of blood, dead. Yesterday, the county was informed and asked for an autopsy and to arrest the murderers.

Child Laborer Abused to Death 230

How Can Human Life Be Settled Privately?

Zheng Xiaohu, the 13-year-old younger sister of Liu Zhengshi, a woman from Yancheng residing at No. 6 Yinghua Lane, Xiaosha Ferry, was taken in at the age of nine as a child bride by Song Laisheng of No. 3 Zhangjia Lane, Hukou Bridge, Hongkou. Song then sent Xiaohu to the Houfu Silk Factory to work. According to Song Laisheng, four days ago, she was abused and severely beaten by a Chen-surname cart driver due to poor work, resulting in serious injuries and death. But it has been three days since her death, and attempts to settle the matter privately have been unsuccessful. What is most strange is that Song Laisheng wants to file a lawsuit because the settlement has failed, but Liu Zhengshi is unwilling to seek justice for her sister. Xu Jinlin, the local bailiff, believed that the matter could not be delayed any longer and reported it to the local court for an autopsy yesterday. However, Liu Zhengshi also went to the court with the bailiff to request that the autopsy be waived. She was severely reprimanded and ordered to await the examination in order to value human life.

Child Swallows Longan Pit and Dies 231

Attention, Those with Young Children

The Gong family, residing at No. 59 Peide Lane, Xinzha Datong Road, Public Concession, had a three-year-old son born in the previous year. He was plump, lively, and much loved. At about 4:00 PM the afternoon before last, his mother was holding him on the table while peeling longans when, unintentionally, the child suddenly swallowed the longan pit. Instantly, the pit lodged in his throat, causing him to moan and choke. His breath was blocked, his eyes rolled up, and his face turned blue. The family was shocked and at a loss, knowing that the situation was critical, and immediately hired a car to send him to the hospital for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was found that the pit had penetrated deep into the trachea and could not be removed. He died at about 9:00 PM. May parents in all circles pay serious attention to this matter.

Fang Kun Attacked by Enemies with Knives 232

Fang Kun, a 34-year-old from Tianjin, is a rogue who specializes in lending money at high interest rates. At about 3:00 PM yesterday afternoon, he was standing at the entrance of Gaofu Lane, under the Laolaji Bridge, when five enemies suddenly appeared in front of him. Two held hatchets, and one pulled out a handgun and pointed it at his chest, declaring, "Rogue, should we spare your life, or don't blame us for not warning you!" After saying this, one of them used a hatchet to chop at him wildly. He was chopped in the left and right legs, and his right hand was chopped, with all five fingers nearly severed. Fang collapsed on the spot. The assailants then fled. Someone called the No. 541 guard post, and they arrived in a car and took the injured man to Renji Hospital for treatment.

It was resolved to notify all members to take note. It was resolved to notify all members that the business license is a certificate for direct taxation by the state and should be exempt from affixing stamps. Because my lawyer took full account of the interests of the creditors, he refused at the time, causing the creditors to misunderstand the general situation and blame my lawyer for refusing, causing the case to be delayed until now without any money being received. Otherwise, a portion of the money would have been received earlier. Or because my lawyer received a certain amount of motion money early on and deliberately delayed the case, all kinds of misunderstandings. This point originally does not need to be stated, because there are ignorant people among the creditors who will inevitably be used and thus make unwarranted accusations." Lawyer Zhou Xiaoan also said that the money was all saved by poor people, and many have committed suicide as a result of the bankruptcy. Now that there is consistency, there should be no more misunderstandings. The creditors are asked to wait quietly for a solution.

The defendant sacrificed the plaintiff's lifelong happiness for the sake of business relations. His vicious intentions and cruel methods are obvious. He should be punished according to law, and a civil lawsuit should be attached, requesting the defendant to compensate for damages of 24,960 yuan. The plaintiff, Xue Qishi, testified the above circumstances and presented several pieces of evidence, including a leaflet, a bottle of medicine, and several shadow play magazines, saying that after I was injured during filming, the Youlian Company took the opportunity to expand its promotion. The bottle of medicine now contains my severed finger section. There are several photos in the shadow play magazine that prove my position at the Shanghai Film Company at the time was not low. When I worked for the Shanghai Company, in addition to a monthly salary of 80 yuan, I would receive an additional 100 yuan for each film I made. Now that I am disabled, my future prospects are cut off, so I am attaching a civil lawsuit, calculating at 130 yuan per month, which should compensate 24,960 yuan for nineteen years. The defendant, Zhao Taishan, testified that this matter happened three years ago. When filming Two Red Butterflies, the plaintiff played the role of the bandit Zhao Dagang in the play, and there should be a scene where he was besieged by government troops. At that time, there were about sixty or seventy government troops, each holding real knives and guns, surrounding the plaintiff for a fight. As a result, the plaintiff suddenly claimed that his finger was injured. At that time, I happened to be holding a knife, so it was suspected that I had cut it. In fact, the plaintiff did not know who cut him. The defendant's lawyer stated that the defendant, Chen Kangran, had also filed a complaint against the plaintiff for extortion, and the case was scheduled to be heard this afternoon. Judge Cheng verified the confessions and ordered the hearing to be postponed for seven days to summon witnesses for further interrogation.

Veteran Throws Himself into the River 263

Unable to Find Relatives, Travel Expenses Exhausted

Desperate for a Living, He Became Pessimistic

The other day, near dusk, a middle-aged man dressed in a grey uniform resembling a soldier boarded Tang A-yin's ferry at the Customs Wharf to cross the river. When the boat reached the center of the river, the man suddenly jumped into the water to commit suicide. His body sank and resurfaced. Fortunately, Tang and others used a bamboo pole to hook him, saving his life. He was then sent to the Water Police Station. Under questioning, he stated his name as Hu Bin, 27 years old, originally from Linli County, Hunan Province, born in Jiangxi. He initially pursued commerce but unfortunately failed, leading him to contemplate suicide. In the 14th year of the Republic [1925], he heard that the Guangdong National Revolutionary Army was recruiting soldiers. Thinking it better to sacrifice his body for the country rather than continue in business, he left his family and joined the Guangdong army in the same year, serving as a soldier in the 9th Company, 3rd Battalion, 1st Regiment, 1st Division of the National Revolutionary Army. In the 15th year of the Republic [1926], the National Government swore to launch the Northern Expedition. Our army entered Zhejiang and Jiangsu from Fujian, personally participating in many major and minor battles. Later, he was transferred to the 1st Company of the Gendarmerie Battalion of the First Route General Headquarters, serving as a gendarme for eight months. Subsequently, he joined the 6th Regiment, 2nd Division, 13th Army, as a sergeant messenger in the battalion headquarters. He was then promoted to platoon leader of the 5th Company of the same battalion. That year, Tang Shengzhi rebelled in Hunan, and the central government ordered a campaign to suppress him. Our army departed from Shanghai and fought in Anhui, Hubei, and Hunan, eventually achieving victory. In the 17th year of the Republic [1928], we returned to Hanyang from Hunan to continue the Northern Expedition, but were ordered to reorganize into the 1st Brigade, 1st Regiment, 1st Group Army. In the 18th year of the Republic [1929], the Gui Clique rebelled, and the central army launched another western expedition. Our army was defeated and disbanded. He was unemployed in Hanyang, living in poverty. Later, seeing that the military headquarters of the Second Route General Commander Liu was recruiting a company of gendarmerie, he applied and was accepted as a sergeant squad leader, serving for several months. Due to illness, he requested leave and returned to Hanyang. Last winter, he came to Shanghai by ship to seek relatives, but after searching for many days without success, his travel expenses were exhausted, leaving him with no means of survival, hence his suicidal thoughts. The police chief, finding his situation extremely pitiful, ordered Detective Huang Songsheng to escort him to the local court at 3 PM yesterday for assistance.
