Special Item

Mr. Fei Tang's Report 266

Summary Translation of the First to Third Compilations (4)

Regarding the issue of Chinese citizens paying municipal taxes, the report highlighted a noteworthy fact: although properties were located within the concessions, they still held original Chinese land deeds and had never been taxed with land tax. Similarly, Chinese-owned houses in the suburbs, built on unregistered land, were not subject to house tax even if the land was incorporated into the concessions and the houses already existed. The report also stated that, according to statistics from October 1930, there were still 6,780 mu of unregistered land in the Public Concession, exempt from land tax. This represented one-fifth of the total area of the Public Concession. Thousands of Chinese houses located on this land were exempt from house tax. The report further mentioned that before 1897, Chinese houses paid higher house tax rates than Western houses, with an approximate difference of two li during most of this period. The reason for this discrimination was discussed, indicating that in the early days of the concessions, Chinese people did not own registered properties, so they did not pay land tax, and their rent was lower, so they paid less house tax. The intention of having different tax rates was to establish a standard for collecting taxes to ensure that the house tax paid by the majority of Chinese people was equal to or close to the land tax and house tax paid by a small number of foreigners. Subsequently, the practice of charging Chinese houses a higher house tax rate than Western houses was abolished. The circumstances surrounding the abolition of this practice were described as follows: after a certain period, the situation regarding land tax and house tax changed for two reasons. First, a practice developed among Chinese people of buying properties in the name of foreigners and registering the land deeds with foreign consulates. Second, wealthy Chinese residents occupied Western-style houses, resulting in the Chinese paying a portion of the land tax and the so-called foreign house tax. Furthermore, with the increase in the number of Chinese residents in the concessions, the annual revenue from Chinese house tax from 1883 to 1887, as mentioned above, was indeed more than the total annual revenue from foreign land tax and foreign house tax. The original basis for charging Chinese house tax two li higher than foreign house tax, as speculated above, therefore disappeared. In 1898, the Board of Works submitted a tax proposal to the annual meeting of taxpayers, based on the opinion that, under the circumstances at the time, Chinese house tax should no longer be higher than foreign house tax. In order to raise additional funds, it was necessary to levy additional taxes, and the Board of Works therefore suggested increasing the land tax to one-tenth of one li and simultaneously increasing the foreign house tax by two li to equalize it with the Chinese house tax rate, while also increasing license fees. In 1898, the report quoted the speech of the Chairman of the Board of Works when the Board of Works submitted its tax proposal to the annual meeting of taxpayers, including the following two sections: the decision to abolish the two different house tax rates was not made without lengthy and thorough consideration. The reasons for initially establishing the two tax rates were examined, and it was determined that the original basis for implementing the two tax rates no longer existed. As representatives of those governing the concessions, and fully aware of our obligations and responsibilities to all sectors, we specifically recommend to taxpayers that we abolish the various tax rates that were previously considered politically fair and convenient. The report also quoted the Chairman's speech at the taxpayers' annual meeting two years later, where he revisited this issue, stating: two years ago, taxpayers acknowledged that the era of levying the same taxes at two different rates had passed, and demonstrated this acknowledgment in practical terms by increasing the house tax on Western-style houses by two li to match that of Chinese-style houses, without further increasing the tax on Chinese-style houses. I firmly believe that the Chinese community will be very grateful for this move, and that our administration will thereby increase its credibility and respect. I believe that you should not forget that most of the Bureau's revenue is paid by Chinese people, and that Chinese people have no say in the Bureau's administration and do not participate in it. Therefore, our goal should be to avoid prejudice and injustice in administration as much as possible. The report indicated that since 1898, there has been no discrimination in taxation between Chinese and foreign residents, except that land holding original Chinese land deeds and houses built on that land before it was incorporated into the Public Concession were still exempt from taxes.

Regarding the issue of Chinese citizens within the concessions sharing the benefits of municipal administration, the report elaborated as follows: In the early days of the establishment of the Public Concession, municipal funds were limited to the most important administrative affairs, such as police, roads, and sanitation. There was no major difficulty in determining the basis on which to assess the demands of all residents for equal enjoyment of municipal benefits. This was because, at that time, the interests of all residents within the concessions were largely the same in the various municipal affairs undertaken. The more favorable treatment received by foreigners was mostly in minor matters, such as the Bund's promenades, lawns, and the public gardens that existed at the time. However, the cost of these facilities was not significant, and the distinction they represented seemed to be habitually regarded as legitimate. Furthermore, after careful consideration, it was believed that the area of such sites was very limited, and if they were opened for general public use, many practical difficulties would arise, so it was also necessary to acknowledge this distinction. But as the Board of Works expanded its functions to engage in other important and less demanding facilities, such as parks, schools, and hospitals, the situation became more complex. The Chinese people's demand to share the benefits of municipal administration, which was initially undertaken specifically for the needs of foreigners, was bound to become a serious issue sooner or later. The ultimate occurrence of the issue of the right to enter parks is an example of this. Looking at the records of discussions in various periods, it can be seen that there were two points of observation on the part of foreigners regarding the two issues of Chinese representation and Chinese citizens sharing municipal benefits, which can be distinguished as historical and civic viewpoints. On the one hand, some foreigners insisted on the principle embodied in the name "Foreign Concession." Focusing on the historical facts of the concession's origin, these people believed that the original intention of establishing the concession was to "carve out" a portion of the territory for foreigners and their families to reside and do business. The gradual development into a major city and commercial center under foreign management was largely the result of foreign entrepreneurship. According to this view, even if there were a large and increasing number of Chinese citizens in the concessions, the nature of the concessions remained as intended, that is, the concessions were originally established for the benefit of foreigners. The Chinese in the concessions were "tolerated" "guests" of the foreigners and not legitimate residents of the concessions. The Chinese moved to the concessions because the conditions within the concessions were better than those outside. In this case, they must be willing to accept the existing situation within the concessions. In any case, in most respects, Chinese residents in the concessions were better off than those outside the concessions. If foreigners retained certain special rights, even if the cost of the facilities was paid for by municipal funds jointly contributed by Chinese and foreign residents, the Chinese had no legitimate reason to express their dissatisfaction. The situation in the concessions must allow foreigners and their families to live comfortably and be well-educated. The living standards of Chinese and foreigners are different. There are things that foreigners cannot live without, but Chinese do not yet feel the need for them. Foreigners are certainly not obligated to provide special benefits to Chinese citizens, such as parks, schools, and hospitals, which the Chinese authorities had not provided for Chinese citizens within the Chinese areas. On the other hand, some foreigners advocated what I call the civic viewpoint, which focused on the fact that the concessions had developed by accommodating Chinese citizens. These people believed that the wealth and prosperity of the concessions were based on the cooperation of Chinese citizens. The presence of a large Chinese population within the concessions was of great benefit to the concessions. With regard to various civic obligations, such as paying municipal taxes and complying with municipal regulations, Chinese citizens had all been subjected. In short, Chinese citizens within the concessions and foreigners were partners and should enjoy the rights that partners should enjoy. The taxes paid by Chinese citizens are the same as those paid by foreigners, and they should have the corresponding demand to share the benefits of municipal administration. In the future, as times change, Chinese citizens will one day be able to directly participate in the administration of the concessions through their elected representatives. The Board of Works currently only represents foreign taxpayers and must do its best to ensure that all residents within the concessions equally enjoy the benefits of municipal tax expenditures. Regardless of whether the concessions were originally established for foreign residence or whether their prosperity was the result of foreign entrepreneurship, it is unfair for foreigners to demand exclusive rights to public affairs paid for with public funds, while disregarding the equal benefits hoped for and needed by the majority of residents who contribute most of these municipal taxes. In other words, if such consultations had been carried out, the civic viewpoint based on the meaning of cooperation between Chinese and foreign citizens would have received more support than the historical viewpoint based on foreign privileges. The policy advocated by Mr. An Diesheng, the former Chairman of the Board of Works, could also have achieved more satisfactory results earlier. During the annual meeting of taxpayers in April 1900, Mr. An gave a speech on Chinese education, stating that "doing for the Chinese what we do for ourselves" was "just and fair" and also "prudent and appropriate." The report went on to mention the issue of Chinese citizens in the concessions demanding to share the benefits of municipal administration and institutions that were originally established to meet the special needs of foreigners. The situation had become intense regarding the issue of admitting Chinese citizens to parks. The issue of admitting Chinese citizens to parks was traced back to April 1928, when the annual meeting of taxpayers finally resolved to open the parks to Chinese citizens under the same conditions as foreigners. The speech of the Chairman who supported this opening proposal was quoted as follows: The park issue is particularly difficult because the existing park area is small and the number of Chinese citizens is large. The Board of Works is well aware that admitting Chinese citizens to the parks will somewhat reduce the enjoyment in the parks. However, in order to maintain the peace and prosperity of the concessions, the Board of Works resolutely urges you to make this sacrifice, which is inevitable in order to resolve a long-standing difficulty. The conclusion of the commentary on opening the parks is as follows: When the decision to open the parks was made, a practical plan was adopted, that is, adults entering the parks were required to pay a small entrance fee to limit the number of people entering the parks and to prevent certain unwelcome classes of people from entering and trampling on the parks. After the parks were opened in this way, it has been proven that Chinese people enjoy visiting them very much. This can be seen from the numbers listed in the statistical tables attached to this chapter. I believe that the park issue should be briefly described because this issue is closely related to the general principles discussed in this chapter, that is, the principle that will be adopted in the future to enable Chinese citizens to share the benefits of municipal administration, and that the benefits of municipal administration or institutions equipped with public funds should be shared by all residents of the concessions on a fair basis. This principle is the principle that was emphasized when discussing the park issue. The long-lasting dispute was resolved by adopting this principle, and the policy advocated by Mr. An Diesheng in his speech on Chinese education in 1900 was put into effect. On the issue of parks, the civic viewpoint ultimately prevailed, and this observation also triumphed on the more important issue of Chinese representation. The resolution adopted in 1928 fully resolved the pressing difficulties regarding parks at that time, and the "long-standing injustice" referred to by the Chairman of the Board of Works was also eliminated. However, the more comprehensive and important issue of how to fully equip parks and sports fields to meet the needs of the large and growing Chinese population in the concessions remains to be resolved. The prospects for this issue, as well as the issues of education, hospitals, and other medical services for Chinese citizens, are not easy because the scope of the measures required to meet the growing needs is very broad.

Casual Talk

World Miscellany 267

— Seafarer

The library of the British Museum in London has a very rich collection of books. Each time books are arranged, forty people are specially assigned to dust them and keep them clean.

The submarine cables in the Atlantic Ocean connecting Europe and America are more than 300,000 miles long.

Children in London pay a lot of attention to gymnastics and sports, but 10,000 children also suffer from rheumatism.

The trend of divorce among Mexicans has also been increasing in recent years. If they can pay a price of 400 gold pounds, they can submit a written or telegram request for divorce, citing unbearable abuse as a reason, and they will be granted their wish.

The number of Americans traveling to England each year is quite large, and the total amount of money spent is about 15 million gold pounds. This money is spent on entertainment, food and accommodation, and does not include the cost of purchasing clothing and supplies to bring back to their home country.

Thomas Marshall, an Englishman, is a blind musician who is proficient in piano. He was recently elected as a member of the Royal Academy of Music. Marshall is the second blind person to receive this honor.

A Record of the Unprecedented Middle School Sports Meet 268

— Ms. Ye Hua

Today, people are all talking about the nation. They say, "The country is dying! The country is dying!" They constantly encourage each other, saying, "Save the country! Save the country!" But what is the cause of the country's demise, and where do we begin to save it? I say, the cause of the country's demise lies in the weakness of its people. The way to save it is to strengthen the people. There are countless ways to strengthen the people, but the most important is to build its foundation through physical education. Physical education promotes the health and development of the body and mind, enhances the ability and skills of the motor organs, and indirectly cultivates moral character. In ancient times, our country relied on farming and agriculture, and life depended entirely on physical strength. The Shang and Zhou dynasties fought fiercely and endlessly. Without martial prowess, how could they defend against regret? Therefore, education at that time included archery and horsemanship in addition to ritual, music, writing, and arithmetic. Both civil and martial arts were emphasized. When Qin gathered troops in Xianyang and melted down weapons to cast bells, the lifeline of martial arts was almost severed. However, the followers of Chen Sheng raised the flag of revolt, and the world responded. The ambitious and heroic still cherished martial arts. The Han dynasty valued Buddhism and Taoism, and the Jin dynasty admired purity and indifference. The people were weak and fragile. The barbarian invasions occurred, and from the Tang and Song dynasties onwards, martial arts appeared intermittently, rising and falling. In times of peace, they advocated elegance and watched as the Yuan and Qing dynasties entered China. Our nation withered and declined, unable to survive on its own, which is lamentable. Now, with the rise of new education and the transformation of social customs, physical education is regarded as one of the three major goals of schools. It is used to encourage and train people to wipe away the shame of weakness and timidity in history. The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, in view of this, held an 11,000-meter long-distance race this spring. Then, on the 23rd, it opened an unprecedented joint sports meet for all middle schools in the city at the Chinese Athletic Field. For three days, 519 athletes from 39 national, provincial, municipal, and private middle schools participated, along with 43 honorary advisors, 89 staff members, and mostly male and female students with their jeweled hairpins and swaying dresses who filled the stands in every direction. A magnificent and unprecedented event! The venue was surrounded by a short fence, with bleachers outside the fence. The hosts were seated on the platform. On both sides of the north were hung a pair of couplets: "These people come after many trials and tribulations, we should all recognize the models of many scholars, combining civil and martial arts at the same time; this place is the focus of attention from all over the world, may all show the skills of sons and compete for the first voice of the Far East." To the left of the platform was the band of the Poor Children's Home, about ten years old, wearing black capes and blue and white small velvet balls hanging down from their hats, which was very cute. The north side of the field was the male athletes' rest room, with the female athletes' room next to it. Clothes, blankets, food, and utensils were scattered all over the ground, like after a military riot or looting. Order was maintained by the Boy Scouts. On the second day, 200 new recruits were added to the service, and the order was well maintained. Director Xu Shuangfu, smiling, walked back and forth, receiving guests. Ma Chonggan and Chen Yuyi ran back and forth on the track, working diligently. Most of the competition staff had served in the National Games and were experienced in directing operations. At the sound of the gunshot, each athlete rushed forward like ten thousand horses galloping, like a torrent of anger, exerting their strength, competing and vying to show their skills. The teachers wiped the legs of the winners, the classmates held their clothes for them, the crowd applauded, and the friends cheered. The reporters competed to take photos, and their prestige was solid and unparalleled.

Starting from May 1st, this publication will specially form a "Novel Rotary Club," with famous writers Tianxu Wosheng, Wang Dun'gen, Bao Tianxiao, Jiang Hongjiao, Xu Zhuodai, Yao Suifeng, Zhang Henshui, Cheng Xiaoqing, Cheng Zhanlu, and others taking turns to write various short stories, each approximately 10,000 words in length, all of which will be rich in emotion and beautiful in writing. Readers, please pay attention.

Huang Chu-jiu's Coffin Transfer Account 270

— Sun Choucheng

On the 24th of this month, Mr. Huang Chu-jiu's coffin was moved from Zhizu Cottage to Yongxi Hall. Although no obituary was issued beforehand, there were still hundreds of relatives and friends who went to hold the ropes. It departed at 10:30 AM and arrived at Yongxi Hall at 12:00 PM. Onlookers lined the streets. Here is a record of what was seen to substantiate this account.

The coffin was covered in red felt and placed in the Jiufu Hall. Hanging in front was a portrait of Mr. Huang, lifelike and divine. On the table were offerings of fruit, tea, and rice, but no sacrificial dishes. In addition to the tall burning white candles, there were two bright horn lamps in the middle burning electric lights. The flower wreaths piled up like a mountain under the platform. The elegiac couplet presented by Xiaolai was quite special, reading: "Dressed with elegance, twenty years of ambition to chart the world" and "Returning to the origin of ninety-nine, empty hands to the Yellow Springs." It not only perfectly embedded the three characters of Huang Chu-jiu's name but also deeply understood and contained Zen meaning. The couplet I presented read: "With the magnanimity of Uncle Du, he was a philanthropist and also an industrialist, his reputation worthy of inclusion in the Biographies of Money-makers" and "Tao Zhu took and gave with discretion, creating a new world, achieving a great world, his unique vision building a talent pool." Soon, Zhu Ziqiao also came, saying that Mr. Huang was fond of doing good deeds during his lifetime. In addition to running the Chu Jiu Hospital himself, he also enthusiastically donated money for disaster relief in various provinces and for epidemics in this port. Because he presided over charitable causes, he had made his acquaintance. He happened to be in Shanghai yesterday due to the Shaanxi disaster issue, so he came specifically to offer his condolences to fulfill their friendship. At 10:15 AM, Yu Qiaqing came and said that he arrived home at 3:00 AM last night. Today, he originally intended to get up late, but because it was his old friend's last day, he had to come to see him off. Each person holding the ropes was given a commemorative badge made of celluloid, with a half-length portrait of Mr. Huang and the words "Huang Chu-jiu's Funeral Commemoration" on it. Other staff members of the Sino-French and Sino-Western pharmacies and the Great World wore white belts around their waists to express their mourning. At the funeral, two square white flags with yellow characters, four feet in size, led the way. The characters were made of black velvet and were very striking. Behind were four small flags decorated with spearheads, inscribed with words like "Sacrifice," etc. Those holding these flags wore uniforms and rode horses. The entire staff of the Great World and the Sino-French Pharmacy sent four ten-thousand-people umbrellas, yellow satin embroidered with blue characters, and embroidered with words like "The crane chariot returns to the west," "His voice and appearance are still here," "Heaven does not spare," and "Painful loss of a mentor." Behind the umbrellas were dozens of satin sacrificial flags presented by Mr. Huang Jinrong, Mr. Du Yuesheng, and Mr. Zhang Xiaolin. The hearse, car number 8034, had a yellow character made of fresh flowers tied to the front of the car. Onlookers along the way, having heard of Mr. Huang's name but never having seen him in person, all rushed to the side of the car to pay their respects to the remains. There were a total of six military bands, wearing different colored uniforms. Hundreds of flower wreaths, with smaller ones carried by one person with two. The French Concession Chamber of Commerce and the Pushan Villa and other groups all sent plaques. The Chinese Pharmaceutical Association sent a plaque with the four characters "Medicine and stone are ineffective," which caught everyone's attention. The men holding the ropes all held long incense sticks and walked, while the women, in addition to having their own cars, also had twenty yellow cars following. After arriving at Yongxi Hall, the coffin was unloaded from the car of the Universal Funeral Parlor and carried to Room Zhen No. 22, where a table was set up for worship. There were many people and the entrance was somewhat crowded. Wang Meiyu, Chen Shanfu, and other female actors wore cheongsams and white belts, their eyes sleepy and drowsy. They said they had never gotten up so early. After the worship, they went to the Zhuangyuan Restaurant in Baxianqiao for lunch. The consensus was that he had been generous in making friends and courageous in doing things during his lifetime. Although the bank's closure and the resulting turmoil after his death, as well as the risky operation of speculative ventures and failure, were different from absconding with funds, it was hoped that his estate would be sold off to maintain the interests of creditors and comfort Mr. Huang in the afterlife.

Chaplin's Determination 271

— Caoshi

The new film "City Lights" by the comedy king Chaplin, recently awarded the French medal, has comedy music but no dialogue. Countless small jokes are melted into one big comedy, and countless small expressions are woven into an artistic drama. One can appreciate its novel jokes and also appreciate its profound meaning, leaving a memorable aftertaste. Once released, European and American countries hailed it as a masterpiece that dialogue films cannot match in art. However, people know its success but do not know the pain it took to achieve it.

When dialogue films surged, Chaplin wanted to engage in filming his new film. However, he opposed this new invention of science with all his might, saying that sound music was acceptable, but dialogue was not. Because actors, when performing a drama, if they want to take care of their tone and language, they cannot have sufficient expression, which loses the essence of art. Moreover, the world's languages are different. Even if English is popular, it is still not necessarily understood by everyone. Only facial performances can move all of humanity. After this statement was published, although supporters accounted for eight or nine out of ten, there were also one or two who opposed it. Chaplin believed that the persuasion of words was not as powerful as taking a work as an example. Therefore, he made a great determination to use his private funds of US$1.5 million to personally and secretly engage in the planning of the allegory, jokes, material selection, sound matching, and music matching of his new film. It took two years to begin filming, and it was finally published in January of this year. The results were indeed as such, and Chaplin's determination was not in vain.

Correction: The word "諗" under the title "Record of the Origins of the Huan Shang Master's Party and State" the other day was a misprint. Also, the number under the Indian Travelogue was a misprint of "33" instead of "35." This is hereby corrected.

Record of Character Decomposition 272

— Manyin

Divination is now regarded as a superstitious matter and is not discussed by enlightened people. However, the art of character decomposition, I do not know when it began. People use it to divine good and bad fortune, and their words often hit the mark subtly. Their so-called "touching the opportunity" is only a few words, responding to the sound and proving effective. Moreover, those who are skilled in this art must also have something in their chest to be able to answer fluently. Therefore, people in the intellectual class regard it as a samadhi of games. There is a certain astrologer in the capital who is also skilled in character decomposition. Every day, his door is like a market, and he writes non-stop from morning to night. A certain friend of mine in a certain institution had just obtained a position, but it was canceled in less than a month. He tried to inquire about it and obtained the character "費" (fei, expense), but he was not told what it was about. He only said that he was planning something. He added a "宀" (roof) above the character "貝" (bei, shell), saying that the matter being planned was related to the government. He added a "母" (mu, mother) to form the character "費" (fei, expense), but it could have been carried through. However, the top of the character "費" (fei, expense) is a "弗" (fu, not), so it cannot be carried through. He added a "宀" (roof) to the character "貫" (guan, penetrate) to form the character "實" (shi, real), and then added the character "弗" (fu, not) to become the two characters "弗實" (fu shi, unreal), which meant that although you obtained the position, it was not real. A certain lawyer was campaigning for the national election and asked someone to decompose a character on his behalf. He also went to inquire and obtained the character "暉" (hui, sunshine). He added a "走" (zou, walk) under the character "軍" (jun, army) to form the character "運" (yun, luck), which meant that this matter was in the process of movement and running (at that time, he was not told what it was about, but only that he was planning something). In the character "暉" (hui, sunshine), the "日" (ri, sun) radical was added to form the character "春" (chun, spring), saying that this could be revealed at the end of spring. There were many accurate hits. There was also a certain person who inquired about marriage matters and obtained the character "蝠" (fu, bat). He frowned and said that marriage is originally a matter of happiness, but you obtained the character "蝠" (fu, bat), and the happiness has been half-eaten away by insects. In fact, the person was already in the process of divorce proceedings. There was also a certain relative of mine who had a minor illness. A certain relative of his passed by a character decomposition stall in Shanghai and saw a large crowd of onlookers. He also tried to pick a character, and he picked the character "及" (ji, reach) to ask about what was happening. So, he asked about the illness. The character decomposer said that the person would surely die. When asked why, he said that the character "及" (ji, reach), when decomposed, opens up to form the character "人" (ren, person) and the character "了" (liao, finished). The matter of being a person is finished. Indeed, his relative's illness eventually did not improve. There was also someone who decomposed the two characters "夏超" (Xia Chao) for good and bad fortune. He picked up his pen and judged, saying, "One" person "selfishly" wants to rebel ("反") (the above is the character "夏" (Xia)). Later, he also wanted to "escape" ("走"), but it was too late and he was already under the "knife" ("刀") "mouth" ("口") (the above is the character "超" (Chao)). In just a few words, the final fate of Xia Dinghou was fully encompassed. Confucius said, "Even small paths have something worth seeing." Truly these words are trustworthy.

Indian Travelogue (37) 273

— Linghua

Returning, we still passed in front of the Kali Temple, where we saw several wooden frames with many people holding sheep for sacrifice. The sheep were hung on the frames and cut in two with knives, the blood flowing all over the ground. Beside them, cows lay peacefully, and people offered flowers in front of the cows. Mencius once said, "Why choose between cows and sheep?" Now, observing Hinduism, they greatly choose, regarding cows as sacred and offering flowers, while regarding sheep as sacrificial animals and killing them. It seems there is fortune and misfortune. Although they think sheep are useless and cows are useful, cows are the representatives of labor, so it is appropriate to sanctify them.

The surrounding area was full of stalls selling miscellaneous items and Kali portraits. I asked my Indian friend to select and purchase several pages and asked him to explain them to interpret Indian mythology and philosophy. However, while walking, I repeatedly felt the pain of being surrounded by beggars. It is estimated that there were no less than one or two hundred beggars around this temple, more than the beggars at the City God Temple in Shanghai. I remember that the beggars in China are most prevalent in places such as Beiping. At Shijiazhuang Station, there were dozens in a row. When I went to Luanzhou, I passed through small markets where beggars were also in groups. Mr. Sta said that the beggars in Moscow, Russia, were also organized into a brigade. I don't know what the lives of ordinary people are like in Russia after it was red. I also don't know what the number of beggars is like in the north of our country after the revolution. I hope those in power will pay attention to it.

Returning, we passed by the Indian Museum. I had visited it before, but I heard that the art museum was also attached here, so I entered through its door again and saw various sculptures and portraits. Observing Indian portraits, some resemble the styles of Egypt, Judaism, and Islam. Their attitudes are grand and close to nature. The faces of women are all made round. Chinese portraits are slightly closer to rectangular, and the lower jaw is slightly thin to express elegance. The Indians are quite plump, but this is not necessarily the case in reality. There was a statue of a goddess using a lion to eat a demon, with two female children serving by her side. It is said that one plays the piano as the god of music, and the other holds an object as the god of wealth. Two men serve below, one in charge of the army and the other in charge of other matters. It is said that this goddess is Kali, who protects all people and defeats demons. Therefore, the Indian people worship her. I saw that even though they are both of the Hindu religion, the White Tower Temple of the male Buddha Krishna is so clean and rarely sees miscellaneous people, while the goddess's temple is so crowded that it is impossible to insert a foot. It can also be seen that faith is easy to spread, and goddesses are easy to become popular because they are more emotional.

On the 23rd, the British lawyer Mr. Mookerjee arranged for me to visit a Raja. A Raja is an Indian prince. The British have ruled India for more than a hundred years, and the small princes of the past are still there. I heard that there are dozens of small kings in the entire territory, still occupying territory sufficient to preserve their wealthy landlord status. It is said that they still have some troops. They are so happy here that they do not think of Shu, only retaining the position of Duke of Anle. However, their wealthy influence is still very great. I heard that there are many with tens of millions of wealth. The British are good at politics and the law is broad, but like fish in shallow water, they are gradually decreasing. The little king lives in a hotel and is very young, able to speak English, only twenty years old like a child. His speech is elegant. If you travel to the inland, you can visit his country.

At 10:00 PM in the evening, I boarded a train northwest with Xin Han and Mookerjee and ten monks to Sarnath. The Mahayana Buddhist Association chartered a train for not much money, only six or seven yuan per person. Those who came to the station to see us off presented flowers to the monks, and I also shared in their incense.

Dropping Nine Taels 275

Yesterday, the 27th, the gold standard fell again, breaking the major barrier of 740 taels. However, there were occasional fluctuations of three or four taels, and the market situation was still stable. From morning to evening, a total of more than ten taels were lost. Looking back, it almost fell by ten taels. The purchases and sales of the industry were uneven. The early morning was still stable. Almost no changes in the overseas silver market occurred. Later, there were slight advances and retreats, and the trend of foreign exchange became loose, and the listing did not change. Therefore, people's hearts were weak. From 741 taels, it fell to 33 or 34 taels due to speculation by merchants selling. The later market felt even more sluggish because exchange bills were becoming looser. Furthermore, because it was not easy to get rid of spot goods, it finally fell to 31 taels. This morning, the major dealers predicted a long position, etc.

Then, Wanxing bought in, while Hengyu Goods sold out, so there were fluctuations of more than two taels, from 41 taels to 38 taels and five cash. Afterwards, Zhifeng, Yonghengxing, Yuanmaoyong, etc. all dragged in, immediately adding three taels, totaling 36 taels. Youth Garden

A Youth's Confession 317

— Tiehua

Instead of calling it "A Youth's Confession," it would be more straightforward to call it "My Confession," because I am also one of the youth. My public confession may be similar to that of ordinary youth.

I am already twenty-three years old this year. When I wrote the words "twenty-three," I felt unspeakable shame and anger in my heart, and the pen in my hand suddenly felt unusually heavy, as if it did not want me to leave such ink marks on this white paper and publicly tell people that I am twenty-three years old. Sometimes, when I was pondering alone, I always thought that my face was still very rosy and handsome, as lovely as the youth piled on the willow branches. So, when I thought of this, my eyebrows would involuntarily move several times, my eyes would open particularly sharply, and a young hero with heroic posture, handsome appearance, and gallantly riding a horse and drawing a bow would appear in my mind. However, when I looked at the mirror on the desk and touched the stiff beard roots under my chin, I was lost in thought and realized that I was indeed a twenty-three-year-old person.

Thinking of my background, I feel too lonely and pitiful. However, I do not want people to pity me. Although I have tasted some of the anxieties and sorrows and joys and sorrows of the world in the past few years, when I think of turning over the historical records of ancient and modern China and foreign countries, who has jumped from mediocrity to happiness, and who has completed a career in joy? As a member of the human race in the world, I came to be human, especially to work for mankind. I finally calmed down and felt that I was fortunate to be able to reach this point of loneliness. The overlapping scars of the past truly symbolize the greatness of future careers. This great career is precisely to struggle in one wound and one scar. The current difficult environment is also to prevent me from falling, not only to bind me and not allow me to fall, but also to require me to work hard to climb up to the tower of light. Therefore, no matter how difficult it is, even the money to buy books and eat is sometimes worrying, my weak heart is still beating with enthusiasm and does not allow myself to take the path of negativity. Relatives and friends have encouraged me deeply, and I also have great self-confidence.

Although I am now also mixed in a group of college students and it seems that it will not be long before I grab a bachelor's degree, just speaking frankly, I always feel that I should add a question mark to whether my level is suitable for my grade. But I still have very dissatisfied memories of the image that the school gave me. The most important thing is that professors and students are too far apart. Although professors have to run around and deal with all parties for the needs of life, how much knowledge do students actually get for how much money they spend? Regarding this point, I must finally blame myself for valuing the form of a title too much and not really working hard to seek it myself. I am afraid that my shortcomings are precisely in knowing but not doing. On the one hand, I can encourage myself, and on the other hand, I often reveal the flaws of self-abandonment.

My love for literature and art may be the same as other young people. I have always had too little appreciation ability, but just scribbled and hoped to succeed as a great writer. How can there be a day of success in such a blind way? It is useless to just admire Goethe, miss Byron, and dream of Turgenev. A brocade-like mouth can be created, but the stomach is still disturbed and the internal organs are not clear. I am afraid that many great writers will die crying badly.

My cultivation is really too wrong. I have no learning and no skills, but the various habits that I have first acquired will often attack. I want to be romantic, how to be unrestrained, how to show the greatness of life. Sometimes I am drunk on fine wine, and sometimes I want to smoke wildly. I know that all kinds of things will hinder my progress, but I know it and deliberately commit it again and again.

The problem of sex is what I need very much in terms of age, so I sympathize very much with Mr. Ruogu's "Thirst for the Opposite Sex." On the other hand, although I know that my studies have not been completed and there are many aspects that need to be worked hard, I will involuntarily plunge into the whirlpool of love, as if I am afraid of falling behind. Although in the hearts of young people, who doesn't want to have a more decent partner of the opposite sex, experience tells me that the ideal must return to disappointment. Life is complex, a large network woven with many aspects of problems. There must be love and hatred, sweetness and bitterness. How many people can really understand each other? The so-called estrangement will always remain between people. Everyone says this: the development of a career is waiting for hard work, why bother lingering in the suffering of love and forgetting your own future? Really, how can I not think this way? However, I will soon see the people who said such things to me also joining in this trick. I really don't understand what kind of poem it is. Now I vow that I will no longer talk about love. I don't want to suffer this pain of troubling myself. I really want to devote my only energy to the progress of my studies. I hope so, and I hope that I will no longer betray my oath.

Everything comes down to the fact that, like my friends, I am ultimately troubled by economic problems. If it weren't for a friend's generosity to lend me tuition fees, I wouldn't even be able to squeeze into a student's seat for a long time. However, lonely life was already in my expectations. I had already said that it was not worth being self-pitying. I remember having made such an oath last year: "I will forever forget the sadness of the past. It is not worth pursuing the past. Even if the northwest wind blows and my body trembles, it has not weakened my muscles and bones in the slightest. Even if my stomach is so hungry that I fill it with river water to fill my stomach, my will has not retreated in the slightest. I will temper my hard-working muscles and bones and strive to complete the thorny path of my studies, waiting for the time when the Chinese nation needs me..." It's just that a year has passed, and I am ashamed to have failed these oaths.

Needless to say, my failure is entirely due to my vanity. Expecting the light of the future is not a pretty word. From now on, I know how to seize the light that is expected. Not only how to seize it, but also to work hard to start seizing it.

I have written so much subjectively, but I have not exhausted one in ten thousand. There are inevitably many defects in this public confession, but it is only a left coupon for a friend who is following young people to work hard together to move forward.
